<div id="review_971310014" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/971310014" />
    <a title="Amanda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7451210-amanda"><img alt="Amanda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1434101513p2/7451210.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/971310014?book_show_action=true">Jun 18, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amanda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amanda" href="/user/show/7451210-amanda">Amanda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7451210-amanda?shelf=kickass-badass-hero">kickass-badass-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7451210-amanda?shelf=stoic-hero">stoic-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7451210-amanda?shelf=favourite-2014">favourite-2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7451210-amanda?shelf=assassin-mafia-hero">assassin-mafia-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7451210-amanda?shelf=romantic-suspense">romantic-suspense</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer971310014" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1216869171472504011">This is one of my old time favorite by Linda Howard. Reading it again after all these years never seemed to diminish my love for this book. Cry No More is one of the best romantic suspense I've ever read.<br/><br/>The heroine, Milla Edge - a mum desperately seeking for her child who was abducted from her own hands when he was just over a months old. For ten years she never give up hope and in the meantime she set up a volunteer group to help others in her predicament. <br/><br/>The hero, James Diaz - an assassin, a</span>
  <span id="freeText1216869171472504011" style="display:none">This is one of my old time favorite by Linda Howard. Reading it again after all these years never seemed to diminish my love for this book. Cry No More is one of the best romantic suspense I've ever read.<br /><br />The heroine, Milla Edge - a mum desperately seeking for her child who was abducted from her own hands when he was just over a months old. For ten years she never give up hope and in the meantime she set up a volunteer group to help others in her predicament. <br /><br />The hero, James Diaz - an assassin, a bounty hunter or a vigilante? He seems shadowy and his true motivation behind the work he had done over the years was not clearly explained to me. But I'm captivated by his personality. A man who isn't verbal, but let action speaks for himself. After he found out that the smuggling ring that Milla looking into coincide with his own interest, he decided to help her locate her lost child. Though we never got his POV, I think he admire Milla's spirit and love the sense of accomplishment when he could help someone in need.<br /><br />For me, a perfect romantic suspense is when the author can make me rooting for the couple and at the same time feeling engage with the suspense plot as well. From the beginning, I'm so invested with Milla and her struggling for justice. I wanted her to find her son back. With little clues thrown along the way, she stumble nearer and nearer to the truth. I'm totally at edge and wondering who is the bad guys.<br /><br />As for the romance, what I like most of the absence of anything insta. I felt that too many romantic suspense use the insta-lust way to speed things up. Milla and Diaz initially encounter was hostile and she was kinda freaked out by his reputation. But she decided to risk it and tried to get the help from this infamous assassin. I enjoyed their slow pace of getting to know each other and doing the sleuthing tasks together. There isn't a lot of flowery speeches considering Diaz was pretty uncommunicative kind of man, but you will just feel in love with him. <br /><br />I love the ending and the epilogue. Is not what I would have envisioned in the beginning, but is still perfect in every way leaving you closing the book with happy tears. <br /> <br /><b>"It's okay to live. It's okay to be happy again."</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="1216869171472504011" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText16916606875999607522" style="display:none">I liked this, up until the end and then when the blobfish pustule H betrayed the h by destroying her son's information, I was reaching for the Captain and a skillet. There is no way I believe a woman who searched so hard and so long would forgive that action - no matter how good a pike poker he was. <br /><br />I also have serious doubts about any adoptive parents who get into a situation where they have a kidnapped child and don't let that child know or get to know the rightful parents. That was 100% fertilizer in my estimation. Do you really want people like that raising a kid? I sure as heck did not.<br /><br />I can see not pulling the kid from his innocent family, but srsly - they bought a baby, yet they werent' suspicious? Also the h and her ex husband should have gotten visitation at least. LH gives us nothing on the rage and problems that kid must have felt when his adoptive parents told him the truth all those years later. <br /><br />Anyhows, the end ruined the rest of it and I wanted the H to die by a toilet seat to the head.</span>

  <span id="freeText15147023098816772818" style="display:none">5 darn stars<br /><br />Devastating, gut wrenching, intense and filled with so much suspense(and heart!). This book was written so darn well i only put it down once at work (even then i kept thinking about Milla and her unimaginable loss) I like heroines like Milla. Strong hearted, strong willed, stubborn and fights her own cause. She was all brains and acknowledged her lack of brawn which made me love her even more because the action scenes were then more realistic. She meets someone who fights along with her and the attraction there was spot on. I loved the hero here. He was mysterious, aloof and cold, only showing his bright spark to Milla and Milla only. He was possessive, he was sexual and he was scary! <br /><br />That prologue made my heart sink....and then around 15% towards the end of the book- that had me in LITERAL tears. I don't think i've choked up in tears for a book in a while and this one did it for me. **round of applause**<br /><br />HIGHLY, HIGHLY RECOMMENDED!</span>

<div id="review_234132228" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/234132228" />
    <a title="Mei" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6876967-mei"><img alt="Mei" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1422277196p2/6876967.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/234132228?book_show_action=true">Nov 26, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mei" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mei" href="/user/show/6876967-mei">Mei</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6876967-mei?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer234132228" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4794987578727741287">This book was recommended to me by Linda e Mo same as the <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12716613.The_Witness' title='The Witness by Nora Roberts' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Witness</a> that I liked very much. This was a solid book too, but not as good as that one.<br/><br/>It's about the heartbreaking story where a child is stolen and the mother has been looking for it for 10 years without success, loosing the father, the man she loved and who loved her, due to that search.<br/><br/>It was really well explained, but there was an overabundance of inner monologue. We are constantly inside Milla's, the mother, head. Even in the mi</span>
  <span id="freeText4794987578727741287" style="display:none">This book was recommended to me by Linda e Mo same as the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12716613.The_Witness" title="The Witness by Nora Roberts" rel="nofollow noopener">The Witness</a> that I liked very much. This was a solid book too, but not as good as that one.<br /><br />It's about the heartbreaking story where a child is stolen and the mother has been looking for it for 10 years without success, loosing the father, the man she loved and who loved her, due to that search.<br /><br />It was really well explained, but there was an overabundance of inner monologue. We are constantly inside Milla's, the mother, head. Even in the middle of a dialogue, we get to see what Milla's thinking, so I had to backtrack to catch the actual dialogue! It was annoying!<br /><br />Also the hero, Diaz, was too dark for me. I cannot say that he's a negative character, but he was so cold that I just couldn't like him as I wish to like my heros....<br /><br />Still the story is good and it's realistic enough to be truly awful because something like that could and do happend in real life!<br /><br />For me this was a 3,5 stars rounded to 4!</span>
  <a data-text-id="4794987578727741287" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_984655582" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/984655582" />
    <a title="♥Rachel♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5481477-rachel"><img alt="♥Rachel♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1363996055p2/5481477.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/984655582?book_show_action=true">Jul 02, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="♥Rachel♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="♥Rachel♥" href="/user/show/5481477-rachel">♥Rachel♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9781590861691" href="/book/show/2012698.Cry_No_More">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5481477-rachel?shelf=audio-book">audio-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5481477-rachel?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5481477-rachel?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5481477-rachel?shelf=romantic-suspense">romantic-suspense</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer984655582" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11742521065256124293"><b>Cry No More</b> was published more than ten years ago, but that hasn’t diminished the appeal at all! It brought out a range of emotions in me. It was a heartbreaking tale, any mother would probably gasp after the first chapter, but it was also an exciting, action packed read! Let’s not forget the romance, because as usual, it’s my favorite part! <br/><br/>Milla’s life was forever changed ten years ago, and since then she’s been a women with a mission. For the last ten years Milla has been the front woman for </span>
  <span id="freeText11742521065256124293" style="display:none"><b>Cry No More</b> was published more than ten years ago, but that hasn’t diminished the appeal at all! It brought out a range of emotions in me. It was a heartbreaking tale, any mother would probably gasp after the first chapter, but it was also an exciting, action packed read! Let’s not forget the romance, because as usual, it’s my favorite part! <br /><br />Milla’s life was forever changed ten years ago, and since then she’s been a women with a mission. For the last ten years Milla has been the front woman for <b>Finders</b>, an organization that helps locate missing people. She’s been relentless in her pursuit, and driven by a past tragedy to the point that her personal life has basically become nonexistent. That is until the mysterious and enigmatic Diaz comes into the picture. She’s been on his tail for years after hearing he possesses the information she’s been tirelessly searching for. <br /><br />I can totally understand why Milla would basically let her entire life go to focus on her goal, but I was sad to see her lose such a happy situation. Seeing others move on broke my heart and it did break Milla’s heart when she allowed herself to dwell on it, so I was thrilled with Diaz coming into the picture. Their romance wasn’t planned by either of them, but isn’t that when you find the absolute best, when you’re not looking for it? These two just <i>fit</i>. I love how the character weren’t the most beautiful, gorgeous, rich people around. Milla is described as pretty but not in a typical way, possessing something about her that made her graceful, and attractive; a certain intangible quality that would drew people to her instantly. Just the presence of Diaz made people wary and scared. His remote, cold gaze, set alarm bells ringing, but there was something very compelling about him to Milla, and from the moment they meet there’s chemistry. He’s very <i>male</i> and exudes the kind of power where people take notice.<br /><br />The romance was just part of the story and Milla’s relentless pursuit of the truth has put her in danger now that she’s come so close to discovering it. I had suspicions early on and when they were confirmed I wanted to shake these people I was so angry! <br /><br />Linda Howard has written many stories, but she is a new author to me. This is the second book I’ve read by her, and while I did love <b>After the Night</b> just a little more, <b>Cry No More</b> was an outstanding, compelling story! Romantic suspense at its best! <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11742521065256124293" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4065244859592785512"><b>FOUR AND A HALF STARS!</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1408972967i/10916533._SY540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>If I had a whole week to convey my feelings for this book, I just wouldn't have enough time to write an appropriate review.   <span id="freeText4065244859592785512" style="display:none"><b>FOUR AND A HALF STARS!</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1408972967i/10916533._SY540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>If I had a whole week to convey my feelings for this book, I just wouldn't have enough time to write an appropriate review. As a re-read, I didn't think I would be so enamoured with this book, but once again, I'm reminded why Linda Howard is a go-to author for me.<br><br><i>Cry No More</i> is the heart wrenching story of one mother's search for her lost baby. Milla Edge was left for dead after her new born baby was kidnapped in a blitz attack at a market in Mexico. Ten years later, armed with one less kidney, unsupportive family and a dissolved marriage, Milla's entire life has devolved into two words: Find Justin. Every stone that needed turning had been turned, every rumour whispered had been determined, yet Milla has been unable to find a solid lead that will help her reach her goal of finding Justin. That is, until an anonymous tip leads her to Guadalupe, where she crosses paths with the mysterious Diaz. As they uncover truths that have been hidden for ten long years, Milla must face her own stark reality; some things in life just aren't meant to be.<br><br>I cannot tell you how much I enjoyed this book lest this morphs into an epic nerd gush that may make you uncomfortable. Instead, I'll give you the bare bones of it: excellent pacing, great action, a swoon-worthy hero, a strong female lead who takes out the mother of the decade award and writing that will inspire strong emotions in even the hardest of hearts. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[My only minor quibble with this book (and by minor I mean almost non-existent) is that I wish this book had a little more sex in it. Definitely a book you must read at least once.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_26825684" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/26825684" />
    <a title="Christa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/261662-christa"><img alt="Christa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1524003029p2/261662.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/26825684?book_show_action=true">Jul 09, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christa" href="/user/show/261662-christa">Christa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780345453426" href="/book/show/626082.Cry_No_More">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/261662-christa?shelf=i-own">i-own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer26825684" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer37268914056588012">I thought that Cry No More was an absolutely wonderful book. It was one of the most emotional that I have read in a long while. The book was humorous in places, heartrending in others. The heroine, Milla, has spent the last years devoting herself to Finders, the organization she founded to locate missing children. Diaz, a shadowy, dangerous figure who has the reputation of being able to find anyone, appears in Milla's life after she begins asking questions about him. The two team up to unravel t</span>
  <span id="freeText37268914056588012" style="display:none">I thought that Cry No More was an absolutely wonderful book. It was one of the most emotional that I have read in a long while. The book was humorous in places, heartrending in others. The heroine, Milla, has spent the last years devoting herself to Finders, the organization she founded to locate missing children. Diaz, a shadowy, dangerous figure who has the reputation of being able to find anyone, appears in Milla's life after she begins asking questions about him. The two team up to unravel the truth behind events that changed Milla's life. <br /><br />Milla was an incredible heroine. She was naturally a sweet, ultra feminine person, but she turned herself into a tough survivor who could withstand tragedy. Her own torment and anguish was used by her to help others. Diaz was almost as unlikely a hero as could be imagined, but he was a great one. He was tough, strong, and hadn't ever felt emotionally connected to others. He and Milla felt an attachment to one another almost at once, and he was immediately very protective of her. The relationship between these two was very passionate and steamy, but also poignant and sweet. <br /><br />This book was fastmoving and riveting, while being incredibly touching. Expect emotional ups and downs in this one, and prepare for some gut wrenching moments.</span>
  <a data-text-id="37268914056588012" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('t2pQXiLIaquQW40UzWMXGjb3ddd3MfKfAoQ7F5YBrpKkJSvnb+CEps8OzMUKYCfka4f0pvSw8kvHsirr3q3WKQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('gakXQ+bses1u/0VQOuetgqP+WF7z3JWf6P7wQzMMCvyS5mz6q8SUwDGqBIH95J18/o7ZL3BdlUstyOG/e6ByRw==')})
  }
//]]>

Ben’s charged with finding Heidi’s killer, and keeping his relationship with Jade a secret. \n\nJade Donovan has spent the past five years teaching lessons and training horses, leaning on the unswerving support of gay best friend, Jeremy, as she raises her daughter, Clara, alone. When she finds Heidi\'s body, Ben crashes back into her life, and she’s too rattled to steel herself against his dark, stern magnetism. She needs him, she realizes, to hold at bay the terrifying evil that lurks in the shadows, claiming the lives of little girls.\n\nAs the dark nights close in around them, they cling to the tatters of their relationship; Ben risks his job, and Jade risks her heart in the search for justice, keeping the daughter they both love safe.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"10656220075456331538\" href=\"#\" <span id="freeTextContainer538140303863757143"><i>Librarian Note: There is more than one author in the GoodReads database with this name.</i><br/><br/>Linda S. Howington is an American best-selling romance author writing under the pseudonym Linda Howard. After 21 years of penning stories for her own enjoyment, she submitted a novel for publication which was very successful. Her first work was published by Silhouette in 1982. She is a charter member of Romance </span>
  <span id="freeText538140303863757143" style="display:none"><i>Librarian Note: There is more than one author in the GoodReads database with this name.</i><br /><br />Linda S. Howington is an American best-selling romance author writing under the pseudonym Linda Howard. After 21 years of penning stories for her own enjoyment, she submitted a novel for publication which was very successful. Her first work was published by Silhouette in 1982. She is a charter member of Romance Writers of America and in 2005 Howard was awarded their Career Achievement Award.<br /><br />Linda Howard lives in Gadsden, Alabama with her husband, Gary F. Howington, and two golden retrievers. She has three grown stepchildren and three grandchildren.<br /></span>
